Local News

Citywide Martial Law Yesterday for Communist Party Anniversary

▲···········▲

Slight Disturbances in the Concession

Peace in the Chinese Area

Yesterday was the 15th anniversary of the founding of the Soviet government. The Communist Party organizations in this city had secretly plotted activities. The authorities in the Chinese and concession areas had received early reports and taken unusually thorough precautions. Therefore, the Nanshi and French Concession areas were as quiet as usual. However, there were slight disturbances in the International Settlement. The situation in various places yesterday is recorded as follows:

International Settlement

At about 11 am yesterday, between Beijing Road, Zhifu Road, and the Northern Mud City Bridge, near the Sino-French Pharmacy, two men dressed in blue cloth shirts and pants, resembling workers, stood at the intersection of Beijing Road and Zhifu Road, holding red flags and firecrackers. There were more than a hundred people resembling workers and students on both sides of the road cheering them on. The workers holding the flags waved them to direct the crowd, shouting slogans and setting off firecrackers, followed by applause. As a result, nearby residents and businesses were slightly frightened. The patrol officers at that location immediately blew their whistles and rushed into the crowd to make arrests. Nearby patrol officers also arrived after receiving the information. They arrested one person each resembling a student and a worker. The others had already scattered and fled. The police car from the Laoza Gate Police Station also arrived and took the two people to the police station for interrogation.

French Concession

Yesterday, patrol officers in the French Concession wore helmets and patrolled back and forth. At the iron gates where the Chinese and French concessions met, more patrol officers were stationed to maintain strict vigilance. As a result, only in the quiet areas of the western section were red reactionary leaflets and various slogans discovered. No disturbances occurred.

Zhabei

After receiving orders to prepare for defense, the Fourth and Fifth Districts of Zhabei cooperated with the Municipal Security Team to maintain vigilance. They paid particular attention to pedestrians. In the evening, they implemented a factory curfew, and all public entertainment venues were ordered to close to avoid mixing with the crowd. In addition to the armed police stationed in the North Railway Station area, the Municipal Security Team also stationed double guards at various key points. The defenses at the intersection of Baoshan Road and the Chinese and concession areas were particularly strict. In addition, there was a patrol team patrolling back and forth, so the order was quiet, and no incidents occurred. Only reactionary slogans were found on the electric poles or walls in secluded places. When the patrol team discovered them, they immediately tore them down and reported them to the district office.

Pudong

The police and militia organizations in Pudong received orders from their superiors in advance to step up precautions yesterday to prevent Communist Party disruptions and other incidents. Zhang, the district chief of the Third District, and Xu, the head of the militia, each dispatched armed police and militiamen to patrol and inspect various important crossings starting at 6 am. The defenses were particularly strict in the evening. At the same time, detectives Zhang Yong and Yang Jinsen led all the detectives to check pedestrians at various key intersections. Throughout the day, the area was peaceful as usual. Only the patrol team of the Third District discovered six or seven small red Communist Party flags and several leaflets on the electric poles on New Market Road. The district reported them to the General Bureau for inspection and verification.

Drastic Drop in Rice Prices; Various Parties Seek Relief

Silver and Money Industries Jointly Raise 3 Million Yuan

Chamber of Commerce Sends Letters to Various Places Seeking Circulation

This year, due to the abundant harvest of grains in the country, rice prices have drastically fallen, endangering the farmers' economy. The central authorities convened a food meeting to discuss relief measures. Jiangsu Province and the two cities of Nanjing and Shanghai specially organized food adjustment associations to seek solutions. After two meetings, it has been decided to set up rural public warehouses in various places to facilitate farmers' loans and mortgages. The authorities in this city are also actively implementing plans formulated by the Social Affairs Bureau. At the same time, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce has also telegraphed the Fujian and Guangdong Chambers of Commerce to investigate the food situation in order to find ways to circulate it.

Planning Warehouse Funds

Since the Jiangsu-Shanghai Food Adjustment Association held a joint meeting last Friday with representatives from Jiangsu Province and decided to establish rural public warehouses, it participated in a meeting of the Shanghai Local Association of Silver and Money Industries last Saturday to discuss funding and loan methods. As a result, it was decided to jointly raise 3 million yuan, with the Shanghai Banking Association undertaking 1 million yuan, the Money Industry Association undertaking 1 million yuan, and banks that are not members of the Banking Association sharing 1 million yuan. The lending institutions will be handled by the local branches of the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and major banks. If there are no branches established, they will be handled by neighboring branches. The warehouses will be jointly organized by fair merchants and branches of the Bank of China in various places. The association also considered that the areas with the most rice production in Jiangsu Province include the 22 districts of Suzhou, Changzhou, Zhenjiang, and Wuxi, and that the Jiangnan area is traditionally wealthy and easier to manage, so it was decided to start there first. In the Jiangbei area, due to various inconveniences such as transportation and financial institutions, other methods will be needed.

Chamber of Commerce Sends Letters to Various Places

In addition to participating in the Jiangsu-Shanghai Food Adjustment Association to actively promote food adjustment and relief of the farmers' economy, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce believes that the fundamental solution is to promote circulation. Therefore, yesterday, it specially sent letters to the Chambers of Commerce in Guangzhou, Shantou, Hong Kong, Xiamen, Fuzhou, Tianjin, and other places, requesting them to investigate the local food situation in order to find ways to circulate it and assist in the adjustment.

Municipal Government Plans Storage

The Municipal Government of this city is also paying close attention to the sharp drop in grain prices. In addition to the Food Committee originally established by the Social Affairs Bureau to specialize in adjusting rice prices, it has now requested the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Interior to pay attention to the import of foreign rice and to find ways to transship it for sale. According to Secretary-General Yu Hongjun yesterday, the Municipal Government intends to establish a large-scale grain storage warehouse to relieve the farmers' economy. The Social Affairs Bureau has been actively planning this, and it will be implemented soon. The content of the plan is roughly divided into three points: (1) The warehouse fund will be separated from the municipal finances and dedicated to handling this matter. (2) The Municipal Chamber of Commerce and financial and rice industry groups will cooperate. (3) Loans or mortgages will be completely aimed at benefiting farmers.

Chen Jiliang Inspects Various Ships at Songkou Yesterday

Scheduled to go to Xiangshan Ocean to inspect tomorrow morning

Commander Chen Jiliang of the First Fleet has been ordered by the Ministry to inspect the navy and various naval affiliated agencies in the Yangtze River and coastal areas. The first to be inspected were the garrison warships in the upper and lower reaches of the Yangtze River. The inspection in the Hankou area has been completed long ago, and the inspection in the Nanjing area was completed on the 4th. Commander Chen immediately took the flagship Hai Chou and arrived in Tongzhou at 8 am on the 5th to inspect the Jiao Ri Survey Ship. At 10 am, the inspection was completed. He still took the original ship and sailed straight to Shanghai, arriving at Wusongkou to anchor in the evening. The inspection of the ships stationed at Sanjiashui in Songkou was originally scheduled for the 6th, but the wind in Songkou was very strong that day, and all the ships sailed to Wusong Town to temporarily anchor and avoid the wind. Therefore, the inspection was temporarily postponed. Yesterday, the wind weakened slightly, and the ships temporarily anchored in Wusong to avoid the wind sailed back to Sanjiashui to be inspected. The inspection was not completed until the evening. The ships inspected yesterday included the Jiankang and Hu ships, two torpedo boats, and the Qingtian and Jiangzhen Survey Ships. Commander Chen has scheduled to take the flagship Hai Chou to the waters of Xiangshan in Ningbo tomorrow morning to inspect the Ganlu and Jingxing ships, and then transfer to Xiamen, Fujian, and other places for inspection. After the inspections in Fujian and Xiamen are completed, he will return to Shanghai to inspect the land-based agencies affiliated with the Fujian Naval Headquarters.

Newspaper Association Holds Banquet Last Night for Professor Martin

Mr. and Mrs. Martin Return to the United States this Morning

Professor Martin, Director of the Journalism Department of the University of Missouri, USA,

was hired by the Journalism Department of Yenching University in Beiping to serve as a visiting professor for one year. He is scheduled to return to the United States this morning. The Shanghai Newspaper Association specially hosted a banquet at Xinghualou last night to bid farewell to Mr. and Mrs. Martin and their son. Those invited to attend from the press included Shi Liangcai, Qian Bohan, Ma Yinliang, and Gu Angruo from Shen Bao; Wang Boqi and Wang Cuwei from Xinwen Bao; Wang Yingbin and Xiong Shaohao from Shishi Xinbao; Huang Bohui and Cai Hangsu from Shibao; Chen Hanming from North China Daily News; Dong Xian Guang from China Press; Powell from China Weekly Review; Mr. and Mrs. Harris from the United Press; Mr. and Mrs. King from the New York Times; Huang Xianzhao, Director of the Journalism Department of Yenching University; and Wu Dao, Professor of Journalism at St. John's University. During the banquet, Chairman Shi Liangcai delivered a welcome speech, stating that Mr. Martin, Mrs. Martin, distinguished guests, and colleagues, today, the Chinese press in Shanghai welcomes Mr. Martin, Dean of the Journalism School of the University of Missouri, and his wife. My colleagues consider Mr. Martin a scholar with mathematical knowledge of journalism. He has taught at the University of Missouri for many years and inspired the younger generation. His contribution is very great. Moreover, because he is an exchange professor with the Journalism School of Yenching University, he came to our country to preside over the Journalism School of Yenching University. Thus, the foundation of the Journalism School of Yenching University, which is still in its initial stages, is becoming more and more solid. It is truly beneficial to the future of journalism and culture in our country. It is a great honor for my colleagues to jointly welcome this famous professor and scholar today. Professor Martin then delivered a response, stating that he had visited China three times before. The courteous and amiable spirit of the Chinese people is well known throughout the world. He has personally experienced it and cannot forget it. He has not made any contribution to the Chinese press. However, he feels that the future of Chinese newspapers will have unprecedented development. His only suggestion tonight is that Chinese newspapers become a major undertaking for public education, analyzing and criticizing current events to enlighten the public. The future of the new China depends on the promotion of newspapers. He hopes they will work hard.

Completion of the Commercial Association Boy Scout Memorial Monument for Sacrificing for the Country

Inauguration Ceremony to be Held Soon

Letter Requesting a Decision on the Memorial Day

The Boy Scout Corps of the Municipal Commercial Association has established a monument for the members who died for the country in the Battle of Shanghai, including four martyrs such as member Wei Yunxiang. The new Jinji Construction Factory has undertaken the construction as a semi-voluntary service. Now it is completed and the memorial service and inauguration ceremony will be held soon. The details are as follows:

Erection of a Memorial

The monument is located in front of the council hall of the Municipal Commercial Association, about eight feet in circumference and about two feet high. It is surrounded by iron railings and topped with the Boy Scout emblem. It faces northeast. The front is engraved with the four large characters "Sacrifice for the Country" inscribed by General Cai Tingkai of the 19th Route Army. A white stone inscription is embedded on the side, written by Wang Xiaolai, Chairman of the Municipal Commercial Association. The text reads: "On January 28th of the 21st year of the Republic of China, the Japanese army attacked Zhabei unsuccessfully and then divided into land, sea, and air forces to attack Shanghai. In order to save refugees and wounded soldiers, this association dispatched Boy Scouts to form rescue teams and set out to rescue them. Members Luo Yunxiang, Mao Zhengxiang, Ying Wenda, and Bao Tingwu, who were non-combatants, were killed by the enemy. This is unheard of in international law. Funds were raised to support their families, and the general circumstances of the four martyrs' deaths were recorded on a stele beside the court of this association to show their loyalty and commend them. Alas, the spirit of Xianzhen has not returned, and the talk of the Hu cavalry grazing south is still rampant. Those who come later, strive for it. The time is the September 18th National Humiliation Memorial Day of the 21st year, and the names of the martyrs are Luo Yunxiang, age 21, from Shantou, Guangdong; Ying Wenda, age 21, from Fenghua, Zhejiang; Mao Zhengxiang, age 19, from Shanghai, Jiangsu; Bao Tingwu, age 18, from Yinxian, Zhejiang."

Selecting a Memorial Day

The Municipal Commercial Association sent a letter to the Preparatory Committee of the China Boy Scout Association, stating that the members of the corps reported that the four martyrs' memorial tower will be completed soon, and that the memorial service should be held as soon as possible. On the 28th of last month, a plan for the memorial of martyrs was drafted and submitted to the Preparatory Office of the China Boy Scout Association in Nanjing and the Shanghai Municipal Council of the China Boy Scout Association for adoption. In addition to the Shanghai Municipal Council, which has agreed to submit it to the meeting for discussion, the original letter and plan are copied and submitted to your association for review. It is proposed to request your permission to urge the Preparatory Office of the China Boy Scout Association to quickly decide on the memorial and commemoration methods, so that the memorial service for the four martyrs can be held as soon as possible. This has been discussed and resolved by the 17th Standing Committee meeting, and a letter has been sent to your association requesting you to quickly review and handle the case. Accordingly, the case is recorded and submitted, hoping that you will investigate and reply to it.

City Chamber of Commerce Convenes Representatives from Various Industries to Discuss Donating Funds to Aid Northeast Refugees

Ten Articles Outlining Donation Methods

Each Industry Association to Establish Fundraising Teams

The Northeast Refugee Relief Association, jointly initiated by all executive and supervisory committee members of the City Chamber of Commerce and prominent figures from all sectors, has already been formally established. Currently, fundraising efforts are underway with great intensity. Recently, the fifth executive and supervisory meeting of the City Chamber of Commerce resolved ten articles outlining donation methods for various industries in Shanghai to aid Northeast refugees. These have been circulated to each industry trade association for compliance. To clarify the purpose of donations to all merchants and residents in the city and to awaken national consciousness, Mr. Luo Qinghua, a committee member and director of the Commerce Department of the Chamber, has been convening representatives from various industries for discussions since the second of this month.

Industries summoned for discussions included shipping, sugar, paper, cotton cloth, yarn, rice, construction, silk, Chinese soap, and 173 other trade associations. Mr. Luo passionately described the plight of the compatriots in the Northeast, who have fallen under the iron heel of the brutal Japanese but are fighting valiantly at the risk of their lives, all to defend the dignity of the Chinese nation and to serve as the last shield for their compatriots in the interior. He argued that if sufficient assistance is not provided, the people of the Northeast will inevitably perish under the merciless slaughter of the Japanese due to lack of support. This would not only mean the loss of land with no hope of recovery, but also that the enemy would surely move their brutal forces to sweep across the Southeast. The pain of national subjugation would be far greater than the Yangzhou Massacre. He pointed out that everyone has a wife and children and a home, and to avoid being slaughtered by the enemy, they should quickly aid the righteous people of the Northeast. Everyone has a heart of compassion, and aiding the righteous people of the Northeast is a supreme act of charity. While it is undeniable that Shanghai's commerce is depressed, he said, the difference between the suffering of our compatriots in the Northeast and our own is like heaven and earth. That we can still live in relative peace and engage in commerce today is all thanks to the struggles and sacrifices of the righteous people of the Northeast. If we truly wish to delay our demise even for a moment, we must generously open our purses and aid the righteous people of the Northeast who are fighting for the nation's survival. Mr. Luo’s earnest explanation and instructions on fundraising methods moved all the industry representatives, who agreed to establish fundraising teams within their respective industries within five days and to subscribe to monthly donations. They each received donation registers and dispersed. It is now known that the association has established a donation affairs unit office within the Commerce Department, assigning Sun Mingqi, Yuan Hongjun, Li Ruzhang, Zhang Yousheng, Xue Jianxin, and others to serve concurrently as staff members. The sugar and other trade associations have also confirmed their monthly donations and have directly remitted them to the designated bank. The donation methods agreed upon at the meeting, as well as the preface to the donation register, are recorded below:

Donation Methods: 1. The purpose of this donation is to aid Northeast refugees and awaken national consciousness. 2. Donation methods are divided into the following three categories: (A) Percentage of store sales, (B) Percentage of employee salaries, (C) Free donation. 3. For percentage of store sales, the minimum donation standard is one-thousandth of daily sales revenue. 4. For percentage of employee salaries, the minimum donation standard is five-thousandths of monthly salary income. 5. Donors may determine the percentage methods themselves. Those who voluntarily increase the standard amount will be appropriately rewarded by the Northeast Refugee Relief Association. 6. For free donations, the Northeast Refugee Relief Association will create donation registers to be distributed by various industry fundraising teams. 7. Donation payment methods will follow the regulations of the Northeast Refugee Relief Association. 8. The above donations will be collected by the Shanghai Northeast Refugee Relief Association and remitted to the Peiping Relief Association, to be managed and distributed under the auspices of General Zhu Ziqiao, with reports from the said association. 9. To facilitate donation coordination with various industries, the Northeast Refugee Relief Association has established a donation affairs unit office at the Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce. 10. These methods will be implemented upon approval by the executive and supervisory committee of the City Chamber of Commerce.

Preface to the Donation Register: On January 28th of this year, the Japanese army attacked Zhabei, and the 19th Route Army rose to resist, wiping away long-standing resentment in one fell swoop. Women sold their hairpins to support the troops, and merchants and industrialists carried baskets of food to comfort them. In just a month, donations reached over ten million yuan, a display of popular sentiment unprecedented in ancient times. Cunning schemers, thinking to take advantage, eventually retreated under oath. Can it not be said that this was the effect of cooperation between the people and the military? What, then, of the Northeast? The border commanders played games with the enemy, the central authorities were cautious, and the valiant soldiers were all withdrawn into the interior. Those who swore not to coexist with the invaders under the same sky were either common people from the fields or battle-scarred veterans who endured hunger and thirst, risking their lives in the borderlands. Their heroism is no less than that of the 19th Route Army, and the hardships they face are ten times greater. They may be called refugees, but they may also be called righteous soldiers. In terms of their circumstances, these righteous soldiers have already experienced the pain of national subjugation and refuse to be treated as subjugated people. Calling them refugees is a description of their reality. Our association's initiative to provide relief is not merely to provide sustenance for the refugees, but to enable them, with their remaining strength, to complete the task of rebuilding the Northeast. The situation of the three northeastern provinces in China is like the head to a person. Without the head, the person cannot preserve his life. Therefore, the loss of the three northeastern provinces means the loss of China. This has already become an unbreakable law. Saving money and scrimping today to rescue the refugees of the three northeastern provinces is to preserve our own future lives. Japan's invasion of Shanghai was not aimed at annexing territory, but specifically at implementing economic aggression. However, we fought to the death, and our assets and homes were reduced to ashes, but we did not care. This is how the men of spirit should be. The three northeastern provinces have already become a place that Japan is determined to seize. The seriousness of this is probably a hundred times greater than the situation in Shanghai. To save our compatriots in the three northeastern provinces, we should at least approach it with the same sacrifice. Perhaps there will be a day when the Qin Dynasty is reborn and the ashes are rekindled. I have summarized the main points briefly to inform the people of the nation. Written on October 10th, the 21st year of the Republic of China, by Wang Xiaolai, Director of the Donation Affairs Unit of the Shanghai Northeast Refugee Relief Association, and Deputy Directors Luo Qinghua and Yan Fang, respectfully.

Legislative Yuan to Review Rejuvenation Public Bond Regulations

City Government to Send Representatives to Capital at That Time

To Attend Legislative Yuan Meeting for Explanation

According to the Central News Agency, the City’s Rejuvenation Public Bonds, for which the City Government had previously drafted public bond regulations and a principal and interest repayment schedule and submitted to the Executive Yuan for review, have been approved by the Executive Yuan and forwarded to the Legislative Yuan for review. The Legislative Yuan has scheduled a meeting this Wednesday to discuss the matter. The City Government has instructed the Finance Bureau to send representatives to the capital at that time to explain everything. Once the Legislative Yuan completes its review, the Executive Yuan can instruct the City Government to comply. It is also reported that the total amount of these public bonds is six million yuan, with a discounted actual receipt of four million eight hundred thousand yuan according to the public bond regulations. However, the Rejuvenation Plan for this year drafted by the City Government requires a total of six million yuan, leaving a shortfall of one million two hundred thousand yuan after deducting the proceeds from the public bonds. The Finance Bureau will need to find other ways to raise this amount. According to Secretary-General Yu of the City Government, speaking to a Central News Agency reporter, there have been many parties who have come to discuss subscribing to the bonds since the announcement of the public bonds. Foreigners have also expressed a willingness to invest. The City Government is open to both domestic and foreign investors, but will operate within the scope of the proposed regulations and will conduct detailed research to select the most favorable offers before making a decision. Therefore, no announcement can be made at this time. As for the use of the public bonds, in terms of relief, they will be used to provide loans for the construction of housing for the common people. This matter will be handled by the City Bank. In terms of construction, they will be used to establish public hospitals, public libraries, and main roads in the city.

Ministry of Communications Stipulates Priority Delivery of Aviation Telegrams

Fees Still Charged at Regular Telegram Rates

China's aviation industry has been developing rapidly in recent years, with applications becoming more widespread. Facilities for flight safety are urgently needed. Items such as weather forecasts for various locations, preparations for airport landings, and requests for assistance in the event of an accident all require rapid transmission. Recently, to enhance aviation safety, the Ministry of Communications has designated a special type of aviation safety report that will be delivered with priority over other telegrams to ensure speed. The reporting fee will still be charged at regular telegram rates. However, the content of the telegrams is limited to the following essential matters: 1. Requests for weather reports before takeoff and replies. 2. Notification to airports to prepare for aircraft landings. 3. Requests for assistance in the event of an aircraft accident. 4. Warnings regarding aircraft precautions. 5. Reporting the aircraft's takeoff time (the number of passengers and cargo may also be included). 6. Other urgent matters concerning aviation safety. The telegrams must not contain unrelated matters or vague and non-urgent phrases. Otherwise, the sending telegraph office may handle the telegram as a regular telegram. The Ministry of Communications issued instructions to all telegraph offices and wireless stations yesterday to comply with these regulations for aviation safety telegrams.

Central Mint to Begin Minting Next Spring

Remarks by Deputy Director Wang Lai-Zhi

After the implementation of the "abolish taels, adopt dollars" system, the Central Mint decided to start minting new dollars to meet the demand. The opening plan and other matters have already been decided. It only remains to wait for the order from the Ministry of Finance before recruiting workers and starting everything. As for the official opening of minting, it has not yet been decided. According to Deputy Director Tu Xiaolai, speaking to reporters, it is likely that minting will begin in the spring of next year. Because the first issue to decide is the silver dollar fineness, this point has not yet been set by the Ministry of Finance, so work can not be started this year.

Recent Situation of Bandit Suppression in Guangdong Province

Published by the First Army Group Communication Office in Shanghai

According to Guowen News Agency, the First Army Group Communication Office in Shanghai published the latest news yesterday regarding the suppression of bandits by the army. Currently, they received a telegram from Chief of Staff Miao Peinan reporting the bandit suppression situation in Guangdong Province as follows: 1. The Xiaobei River area on the Guangdong border has rugged terrain, with many mountains and steep ridges, often serving as a haven for bandits and communists to flee to. For the past two or three months, under the supervision of Li Hanhun, Director of Pacification of the North River, troops have been actively suppressing them, gradually clearing the area. The pacification work is now 80% complete, with only a small remnant of bandits, about 200 people, fleeing into the Yao Mountains. Director Li continues to send troops to encircle and suppress them. Once this group is cleared, the pacification work can be considered complete. 2. Remote counties in Qiongya also occasionally have bandits and communists gathering. When the troops come, the bandits leave; when the bandits leave, the troops come. After Chen Zhang’s army earnestly searched and suppressed the area, there was also great progress. It can be completely cleared this year. 3. Yu Hanmou of the Guangdong First Army has been very effective in clearing and suppressing the Red bandits in the Yingqian area of Jiangxi Province. The long-standing bandit troubles in Sannan have almost been completely eliminated. Zhang Meixin's division has now dispatched a team to capture Shizi Xu, which belongs to Anyuan County, and continues to advance towards Xiaowei. However, there are many blockhouses in the area, making it difficult to attack. Artillery has now been added to suppress the bandit traces. It can be reported that it will be completely cleared soon.

US Wheat Loan to be Signed in Shanghai

Flour Industry Expresses Intent to Use US Wheat

According to the New Sound News Agency, although various sectors are making every effort to request a halt to the second continuation of the US wheat loan to the value of 11 million US dollars from the US Financial Rehabilitation Corporation to the Ministry of Finance, according to reliable sources in the financial and flour industries, the details of the second continuation of the loan have been successfully negotiated and cannot be stopped. In the coming days, representatives from the Ministry of Finance and the US Financial Rehabilitation Corporation stationed in Shanghai will officially sign the agreement and discuss the method of shipping in batches to China. As for how the shipment of US wheat to China will affect the economy of domestic farmers, it is said that domestically produced wheat is generally difficult to convert into flour. Flour companies have always used US wheat, but because it is currently harvest season for domestic agricultural products and the quantity is too large, it is inevitable that it will conflict with reality.

The National Products Exhibition's Examination of Exhibits is Nearing Completion

Now Relocated to the Xiaodongmen Exhibition Hall for Operations

Following the conclusion of the Shanghai National Products Exhibition, a review committee was promptly organized to meticulously examine the products from various factories, carefully evaluate their grades, and award certificates to provide encouragement. It has been learned that the review process is mostly complete, and the examined goods have been returned to their original factories. Only a portion of the products, due to their more complex manufacturing, require chemical testing and research during the review, thus taking more time. It is expected that this will also be completed in the coming days. After all reviews are finished, the review committee will mark the grades on the goods and report to the National Products Exhibition, so that the grades can be entered on the certificates. After the mayor and director of the Social Affairs Bureau have affixed their seals, the certificates will be issued to the manufacturers on a scheduled date. Yesterday, Mr. Cao, who is handling matters for the National Products Exhibition, told reporters that the date of the awards and whether a ceremony will be held during the awards are yet to be determined, because the association’s finances are very tight and this expense is completely outside of the budget. Additionally, the equipment and items displayed in the exhibition hall have all been moved to the Xiaodongmen National Products Exhibition Hall yesterday. At the same time, its branch office at the "Penglai Market" will also be moved to the exhibition hall today. All unfinished matters will continue to be handled on the fifth floor of the hall.

Shandong Province's Soybean Oil Transported to Shanghai: Customs Temporarily Allows Tax-Secured Release

The Jianghai Customs Superintendent's Office yesterday sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, stating: "Regarding letter No. 210, which opened with a letter from the Cereal and Oil Cake Industry Association stating that oil products transported from Shandong Province are taxed as foreign goods, creating an unbearable burden, please forward to the business tax department a request to reduce taxes on the large batch of soybean oil imported by the Chengdu, Hexing, and Lianxing steamboats on the 14th. Pending approval from the Ministry, please allow the tax-secured release of goods or temporary suspension of penalties, etc. Upon investigation, this office previously received a similar petition from the said association, which was forwarded to the customs for review. Subsequently, the Tax Affairs Department replied, stating that if the amount of the security exceeds the tax due, it can be accepted, while awaiting the government's decision. Apart from informing the relevant merchants by customs valuation and assessment, this reply is being forwarded for your information."

Upstream Yangtze Waterway Fees Increase

Fees Increase by Half Starting Tomorrow

Local steamship companies recently received a telegram from Hankou, stating that due to the daily decrease in the Yangtze River's water level from Hankou to Hunan, the passage of ships has become difficult. Yesterday, five companies, including China Merchants, Jardine Matheson, Butterfield & Swire, and the Three Northern Companies (excluding Nisshin Kisen Kaisha), each sent representatives and agreed to increase cargo fares for the shallow upstream section. The public resolution was made that, starting tomorrow (the 9th), the shallow water freight rate will increase by 50% from Hankou to Changsha, Hunan. Cargo shipped from Shanghai to Hunan will have the fee collected in Shanghai. All passengers have been notified.

Andong Port is Frozen

The weather has been getting colder recently, and Andong Port in Northeast China is frozen, making navigation difficult. Local Chinese and foreign steamship companies received a telegram from Andong yesterday, stating that the port river there would begin to freeze on the 12th of this month. Except for ships departing from Shanghai to the Northeast before the 12th, it will be impossible to sail into the ports of An-Ying after the deadline. Therefore, local steamship companies have decided to suspend all Andong routes starting from the 12th, and resume them only after the ice thaws next April.

Japanese Envoy Returns Home This Morning

Yanagihara and Araki Arrive in Shanghai

Japanese Minister to China Akira Ariyoshi purchased two first-class cabins, number two, on the Nagasaki Maru from the NYK Line yesterday, and is scheduled to board the ship at the Wayside Wharf with his wife and secretary Okazaki at 9 a.m. this morning to return to Japan.

In order to increase the handling of negotiations at the Japanese Consulate in Nanjing, the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs has dispatched Foreign Ministry official Yanagihara Keiichi to China, ordering him to assist with everything in Nanjing. Yanagihara arrived in Shanghai by boat yesterday with his wife and is scheduled to go to Nanjing today to take up his duties at the consulate.

Shanghai is a large trading port with many Japanese ships entering and leaving, and there are many maritime disputes. Japan has specially dispatched a maritime affairs officer to Shanghai, with Araki Shigeo taking office. Araki had returned to Japan for a long time due to personal matters, and only returned to Shanghai yesterday to resume his original post as maritime affairs officer.

Jianghai Customs Abuse of Power Incident: Robert Fforde Appropriately Applied for Leave and Left Shanghai

Affairs are Handled by Deputy Tax Commissioner Grio Lee.

Xinsheng News Agency reports that over one hundred trade associations in this city jointly requested the Ministry of Finance to severely punish customs officials, for reasons including the Jianghai Customs’s auctioning of confiscated white sugar, improperly allowing merchants to alter labeled prices on confiscated sugar, withholding the tax-paid bills of lading of Guangyuan Sugar Firm, and misinterpreting the regulations for boats traveling between Suzhou, Hangzhou, and Shanghai, thereby detaining civilian boats traveling to Hebei. According to the Xinsheng News Agency, Mr. Robert Fforde, the Customs Commissioner, applied for leave to return to his home country from July 12th of this year, and did not return to his post until October 9th. Previously, there was a notice published in the newspaper stating that during Mr. Robert’s leave, all affairs would be handled by Deputy Tax Commissioner Grio Lee. Mr. Robert has now made some explanations regarding this situation to avoid misunderstandings. His statement reads that someone in the General Affairs Section of Jianghai Customs improperly allowed merchants to change the labels and auction off confiscated white sugar, withheld Guangyuan Sugar’s tax-paid bills of lading, and misinterpreted the regulations for boats traveling between Suzhou, Hangzhou, and Shanghai to detain civilian boats, etc. The improper handling of these matters was long ago criticized by a group of merchants. However, Commissioner Robert Fforde has been out of Shanghai and back in his home country since July 12th, and only returned to his post on October 9th, which was stated in a notice published in newspapers. It is said that Mr. Robert has always been committed to promoting good relations with merchants, and intended to correct the misconduct of the person in question. Therefore, as long as merchants' opinions and representations do not violate established regulations, he has always tried to accommodate their wishes. The joint petition from over one hundred trade associations in this city mistakenly included Mr. Robert's name, which should be corrected.

Question of Redrawing Boundary in Southern Shanghai

Qin Xitian expresses his opinion

Recently, Qin Xitian, a resident of Chenxing Township, Shanghai County, expressed his views on the redrawing of boundaries between Shanghai and Nanhui Counties, stating: "The Xinnanhui Daily, issue number 243, contains a report that the County Government convened a joint conference of four counties to discuss boundary issues, including a petition from the Nanhui County Magistrate to take jurisdiction over Chenxing Township, which belongs to Shanghai County. Whether Chenxing Township belongs to Shanghai or Nanhui, both belonging to Jiangsu Province of the Republic of China, is not worth discussing. However, any change in administrative divisions should be based on the convenience of the local people as the premise. Chenxing Township is about eighty li east to the seat of Nanhui County, and about twelve or thirteen li west to the new seat of Shanghai County in Beiqiao. Which is more convenient is self-evident. However, I recall that in the first and second years of the Republic, gentry and citizens of Nanhui County, such as Zhu Zihao, proposed dividing the districts and townships of Nanhui County, and combining Sanlin and Chenxing Townships of Shanghai County, to establish another county, with the county seat in Zhoupu Town, to be named Puzuo County. This was approved by Chenxing Township. At that time, Qin Liangchen of Luhui, Pan Shiruo of Xinchang, and Du Shenzhi of Duxing all strongly supported the idea. Although the matter was not completed, the idea had already deeply penetrated the minds of the people. If the previous proposal could be implemented, it would not only conform to the wishes of the people of Chenxing Township, but also to the wishes of the people in the western half of Nanhui County. As for the case of the late Qing Dynasty Governor-General Cheng Dequan, who奏准劃并斗入表内, [T/N: Unable to translate] including the banks of the Central River in Nanhui County to Shanghai County, in 1928 the Shanghai Special Municipality and the Jiangsu Provincial Government agreed that Chenxing Township of Shanghai County and part of Zhoupu City of Nanhui County would be incorporated into the municipal area, with the takeover temporarily postponed. These two cases have not been canceled and may take effect at any time, which should not be ignored."

Local News II

Japanese Goods Flood In to This City

Japanese Cloth Exceeds British Goods

In the past two days, the Asama Maru and Mikasa Maru ships arrived, carrying a total of more than 12,500 pieces of Japanese goods. Apart from cloth and hardware, there were various miscellaneous goods, such as milk, medicines, cosmetics, leather goods, electrical materials, match raw materials, and other luxury items. These were not large quantities of goods. This further proves the recovery of their trade in China and the success of their dumping policy. According to Japanese business statistics, the amount of Japanese cloth shipped to China last month exceeded British cloth by more than 50,000 pieces, accounting for one-third of the total, amounting to more than 165,400 pieces. Japanese businesses are becoming increasingly optimistic about this.

Chinese and Foreign Merchant Ships Suspend Sailings to Northeast China

Lack of Cargo Leads to Business Decline

No Cargo to Load after the Blockade

Since the puppet regime announced that import duties and tonnage taxes would be collected starting September 25th at Andong, Yingkou, and 口(illegible) [T/N: Likely Dalian], all Chinese goods shipped there have been subject to an import tax of 3%, and staples such as soybeans and soybean oil exported from those ports have also been subject to export taxes. After China announced the blockade of the Northeast Customs, Shanghai customers stopped shipping goods to these ports. In addition, the financial freeze has virtually cut off trade. Also, the South China ports now source their soybean oil and other products from the Yangtze River and Haizhou, which are less expensive and avoid double taxation. Therefore, cargo transport between Andong and Shanghai has also been cut off.

British Merchant Ships Reduce Sailings and Change Routes

Since the 918 Incident, the number of ships sailing to the Northeast from Shanghai has gradually decreased. The Huashang Yu Da Steamship Company has been monitored by the puppet regime. Ships such as Zhaoxing and Haichang have also reduced their sailings, carrying only coal. However, Butterfield & Swire, a British company, had specialized ships sailing the Andong-Shanghai route. After the previous ship, the Zhou Shan, sank after hitting a reef, the Chengdu was reassigned to the route. Now, since there is no cargo going to and from Anhui and Shanghai, and it must pay tonnage taxes, the ship has been reassigned to the South China route.

Japanese Nisshin Kisen Kaisha Company Plans to Restart the Yangtze River Liner Service

Waive Passenger Fees to Attract Customers

But the Result is Still Few Passengers

Xinsheng News Agency reports that since the 918 Incident, the Nisshin Kisen Kaisha, a Japanese company, has suffered greatly from the boycott by the Chinese public, affecting its business. Since the January 28 Incident, it has suspended the Yangtze River liner services. Although it has repeatedly tried to restore the services by every means possible, it has had no effect.

Suspended Due to Boycott

The head office of the company is in Japan, and Shanghai is a branch office. Its business is mainly the Yangtze River routes, with nine ships, including the Luoyang, Fengyang, Nanyang, Yueyang, Ruiyang, Xiangyang, Dazhen, Dafu, and Dali, specializing in sailing up and down the Yangtze River; two ships, the Huashan and Tangshan, on the North China route; and two ships, the Lushan and Songshan, on the South China route. Due to the boycott by the Chinese public, it completely suspended the Yangtze River liner services since the January 28 Incident. It tried to maintain services on the South China and North China routes, but suffered huge losses each time. It then resumed services with three ships on the Yangtze River route: the Fengyang, Nanyang, and Xiangyang. The remaining ships were docked at the Huangpu River and various docks along the Yangtze River.

Ineffective Plans

Since the suspension of services, the sailors on the Yangtze River ships have become unemployed. For patriotic reasons, they are willing to sacrifice. Although three ships, including the Nanyang Maru, have resumed services on the Yangtze River, there are few Chinese passengers and cargo on each sailing. Only Japanese transit goods come to China. Each sailing incurs huge losses. All the Chinese workers in the middle-class cabins had to be temporarily reassigned to other jobs. Although the president of the company came to China and made repeated plans to restore services, such as lowering fares, providing armed protection, and making special publicity, sparing no expense, and preparing to fully restore the services on August 1st, the national sentiment of the Chinese people remained strong, making it impossible to implement the plans.

Waive Passenger Fees

Xinsheng News Agency reporters learned yesterday from sources in the shipping industry that the Nisshin Kisen Kaisha has been making every effort to plan and try to restore business. Its latest plan, which has now been implemented, is to waive passenger fees. Passenger fees and freight fees have always been contracted by compradors, who collect the ship tickets (i.e., passenger fees) and freight fees to cover the ship's expenses. For example, the ship ticket from Shanghai to Hankou is 6.5 yuan, but now passengers are charged 2, 3, or 4 yuan, depending on the passenger. Once there is a slight improvement, three ships, the Luoyang, Yueyang, and Ruiyang, will be restored first. Although the poor Chinese passengers are happy to board, there are still only a few passengers and cargo on each sailing. The cargo is still only Japanese transit goods. Therefore, it is still difficult to truly restore services.

Organize Specialized Committee to Study

The banking community in this city believes that the banking business regulations currently in use have been in place for quite some time, and many aspects are no longer suited to recent trends. It is proposed to revise them. The banking community has instructed experts from various banks to organize a specialized committee to discuss the progress of this matter. In the near future, there may be concrete measures to implement.

Central Bank Adds a Remittance Bureau

The Central Bank initially had two institutions: the Issuance Bureau and the Business Bureau, specializing in the issuance of banknotes and business transactions. Now, the Ministry of Finance, to improve the convenience of remittances, has specially established a Remittance Bureau to handle domestic and foreign remittances nationwide. It is now organized and formally established.

Can Executive Committee Members of Two Trade Associations Hold Concurrent Positions?

Municipal Government Consults the Ministry for Clarification Based on the Situation

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, based on a request from the Silk and Satin Trade Association to clarify whether a member representative of a trade association who has already taken office as an executive committee member of Industry A can be elected as an executive committee member of Industry B, has submitted the request to the Social Affairs Bureau, which has submitted it to the Municipal Government to consult the Ministry of Industry for clarification. It is reported that the Municipal Government has submitted the request to the Ministry of Industry for clarification based on the situation. The consult is recorded as follows:

Regarding the matter of consultation, according to the Social Affairs Bureau, it states, "According to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, it states, "According to the Silk and Satin Trade Association, it states, "Upon investigation, if a member representative of each trade association has already taken office as an executive committee member of Industry A, whether they can be elected as an executive committee member of Industry B, our association has no basis for this question and requests instructions and explanations to provide compliance." According to Article 7 of the Association's Rules, it states, "A member representative of the Association shall not represent more than two commercial legal entities or stores." According to its provisions, although it seems to be specifically for restricting store members, the intention of this provision at the time was to prevent the monopolization and manipulation of member representatives. Therefore, the draft rules of the Association at the time stated that one person could represent two places, but only had one vote and one right to be elected. Subsequently, the provision was revised by your bureau as above, so limiting the concurrent positions of store member representatives should also limit the concurrent positions of trade association member representatives. The reason why it was not clearly stated in the articles was for a general overview, using one example to illustrate the rest. Therefore, in fact, if one person represents two trade associations to join the Chamber of Commerce, it will be rejected by your bureau. If one person is elected as an executive committee member of Industry A and then elected as an executive committee member of Industry B, it seems that one person may represent two trade associations to join the Chamber of Commerce and should be restricted. This is one argument. Another argument is that a person representing two trade associations should be restricted from joining the Chamber of Commerce because they may monopolize and manipulate the situation. As for the executive committee member of Industry A and the executive committee member of Industry B, they are completely two positions, and there is no suspicion of manipulation. Also, their talents or reputation may be needed by both industries. Therefore, they should only be restricted from joining the Chamber of Commerce as an executive committee member of Industry A, and the election of the executive committee member of Industry B should not be restricted. This is another argument. Judging by the merits of the matter, the latter argument seems more reasonable. How should the matter be handled? It is requested that you review and approve and instruct the Ministry of Industry for review and instructions to facilitate compliance." According to this, please review and approve the request and forward it to the Ministry of Industry for review and instructions so that we can comply. This consults the Ministry of Industry.

New Infectious Disease Ward at Shanghai Hospital Completed

Open to Patients Starting on the 10th

The Public Shanghai Hospital at Santei Wharf, Duojia Road in Nanshi, is the earliest public hospital established in this city. Over the years, it has treated internal and external diseases with notable success, particularly in the field of infectious diseases, where it has a strong reputation. Since 1924, the hospital board hired Dr. Zhou Chuliang, who studied infectious diseases in Germany under Dr. Friedrich Mummert, to manage the hospital. Since then, he has made many contributions to the field. Several years ago, Dr. Zhou further invited Dr. Sha Yunwu, who studied infectious diseases at Jikei University Hospital in Japan, to assist in diagnosis. The number of patients seeking treatment has increased significantly. Recognizing infectious diseases as an important public health issue in Shanghai and the scarcity of hospitals admitting such patients, the hospital board raised funds last year to construct a new building. Designed by engineer Xu Jintang and built by Xieji Construction Company, the facility is well-equipped, featuring not only patient rooms but also nurse stations, sterilization rooms, food preparation rooms, bathrooms, changing rooms, and toilets. It was completed at the end of last month. Recently, board member Yao Xinzhi, along with construction expert Zhang Xiaoliang, inspected and accepted the building. It is reported that the ward will begin admitting patients on the 10th of this month.

The case of Sheng Ze Cheng and others being sued by their nephews Shao Yunpeng and others for forging the will of their maternal grandmother, Sheng Zhuangshi, and seizing property has been repeatedly heard in court. Wen Hongen, Director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, recently learned that all districts and stations were employing secret agents to assist in arrests. If secret agents are being used, they should be stopped immediately. Failed Robbery Followed by Threatening Letter to Extort the Victim

Shang Wu, a Chinese detective of the French Concession Police, learned the other day that suspicious individuals were hiding in the Hongbin Teahouse at No. 579 Kaifeng Road. At 2:30 PM, he led detectives Zhou Yushan and Liu Shaocheng in secret to apprehend two individuals, including one Tan Qingxiang, and brought them back to the police station. Under interrogation, Tan confessed that he and Zhang Yingjie, Zhang Xiaogui, and others had repeatedly written threatening letters since the 2nd of this month, extorting 5,000 yuan from Wang Shaofu. Detectives investigated and learned that Wang operated the Guangdalong Customs Brokerage at No. 3, Lane 418, Jiangxi Road and lived at No. 123 Taoyuan Fang, North Jiangxi Road. On the morning of the 14th of last month, several robbers armed with weapons broke into Wang's house in an attempt to rob it. The incident was reported, and detectives were dispatched, who arrested the robbers. The robbers resisted arrest by firing shots, and the detectives returned fire, resulting in two robbers being killed and two being captured on the spot. The newspapers provided detailed coverage the following day. At that time, Tan Qingxiang was being treated at the Four Ming Hospital for an illness. Upon seeing the report, he thought there was an opportunity to exploit. He conspired with the two Zhangs to write threatening letters, intending to extort money. Tan was strictly questioned about the whereabouts of the two Zhangs and led the detectives to No. 2 Yuqing Lane, Zhaojia Road, Ximen, where Zhang Yingjie was apprehended, while Zhang Xiaogui was still at large. The two, Tan and Zhang, were brought back to the police station. Yesterday morning, the police lawyer Wang Yaotang presented the case to the Second Criminal Tribunal of the First Special District Court, stating that since the victim Wang Shaofu had received the threatening letters but had not reported them to the police, the detectives only received three threatening letters when they investigated Guangdalong yesterday, as Wang Shaofu had gone to Hong Kong for convalescence. The letters were being sent to the General Inspectorate for handwriting analysis and had not been brought to court. The police investigation into the case was not yet complete, and Wang Shaofu had not arrived, so no formal charges had been filed, and a request was made to keep the suspects in custody. Tan and Zhang confessed to conspiring with Zhang Xiaogui, who was still at large. Judge Wu Tingqi reviewed the confession and ordered that they be detained for seven days for further investigation.

Unlicensed Pig Slaughtering Leads to Extortion

Giving Away a Pig's Head Was Not Enough

Daring to Gather a Crowd to Demand Two Yuan

Zhou Tong from Yancheng, who lived in a thatched shed at an unnumbered address on Qiwupu Road, made a living raising pigs. Because he slaughtered pigs for sale without obtaining a license from the Municipal Council, Gao Zhengqi, a Jiangbei employee of the nearby Health Department, learned of this. On the morning of the 4th of this month, around 10 AM, he secretly went to Zhou's house, claiming to be a staff member of the Municipal Council Health Department, and used this as a pretext for extortion. Fearing him, Zhou gave him a pig's head, and he left. The next day at 5 PM, he gathered a group of ruffians including Luo Decai (also from Jiangbei), and went to Zhou's place again, saying that they needed ten Yuan tou to settle the matter, otherwise they would report it to the Health Department, and Zhou would have to pay a large fine. Zhou asked his friend Xu Congjin to act as a mediator and paid two yuan, and was finally left alone. The other day, Zhou went to the Health Department to inquire and learned that Gao was actually using a false identity and impersonating an employee to extort money. He reported the situation to the Jianlin Road Police Station. The head detective sent detective Ni Baofeng to Fengshan Road, where Gao and Luo were successively apprehended, brought back to the police station and detained. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Third Tribunal of the First Special District Court. The police lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated the facts, saying that Gao Zhengchao claimed at the police station that the pig's head had been snatched away by hooligans and could not be taken to the Health Department to be reported, and that he did not extort two yuan from Zhou the next day. The second defendant, Luo Decai, completely denied the allegations. Therefore, he requested a postponement for further investigation. Subsequently, the victim Zhou Tongren testified to the events, and Xu Congjin testified that Gao Zhengchao had indeed taken a pig's head the first time, and the second time he came with Luo Decai, and he mediated, giving him two yuan, which was true. When questioned, Gao admitted that the plaintiff slaughtered pigs for sale without a license, so he took a pig's head.

to the Health Department to report it, but it was snatched away by hooligans on the way. He denied going to the plaintiff the next day to take two yuan, and equivocated in his other statements. He also hired lawyer Fan Gang to defend him. Luo Decai testified that at that time, he went to the plaintiff to buy two jiao of meat, but was refused and went home, and there was no extortion. He asked for leniency. Judge Zhao Linyu reviewed the confession and ordered that he be remanded in custody for further investigation and questioning.

Throat Slit and Testicles Crushed, Ni Qilang Dies a Tragic Death

A Glimpse of a White Waistband

Leads to Suspects

Ni Qilang, a Chongming native residing at No. 1 Tongji Lane, Lao Xiaopi Lane, Dongjiadu, Nanshi, had no regular occupation and was a low-level loafer. The day before yesterday at 6 PM, he left home. Around 9 PM, he suddenly returned home in a rickshaw, with bloodstains and injuries on his throat and neck. He collapsed and was unable to get up, falling onto the bed. He immediately told his wife, Gong, to quickly call his younger brother, Ni Shaoqian. Seeing the situation, she rushed to call her brother-in-law, but by the time he arrived, Ni Qilang had already died. An examination of the deceased's body revealed that the wound on his throat had become mangled, with flesh and blood blurred, and his left testicle was crushed, and his kidney was also broken, and bleeding. In the deceased's hand was a white waistband, stained with blood. Based on the origin of the white waistband, she suspected that not long ago, a couple from Beisha (now Qidong County), Shen Shuchun and his wife, had been brought to Shanghai by Ni Qilang, and Shen's wife had a love affair with Ni Qilang. The Shen couple suddenly returned to their hometown on the day of Ni's death. It was learned that Shen's couple had recently suffered the loss of elders, so this white cloth waistband was likely Shen's. It was suspected that the death was caused by a love triangle leading to a violent fight. She reported the matter to the First Branch of the First District. Yesterday, they ordered Qin Defang, the local head of the 23rd Pu, to cooperate with the deceased's wife, Ni Gong, and others to report to the court for an autopsy.

Woman Sells Daughter into Prostitution to Support Lover

Prostitute Zhang from Wuxi, 46 years old, lived with her husband Ting Jinfu in their hometown, farming for a living. Two years ago, she brought her biological daughter, named Qindi, to Shanghai to work as a servant. Although she was nearly 50, she still had a strong desire for romance. Soon, she became involved with Wang Caijin, a coppersmith near Yuanyang Hall in the city. Later, because Wang's wife had passed away early, she brought her daughter Maideng to live with Wang as a partner, pretending to be an old housekeeper. However, the business was slow, and the economy was tight. Wang was worried day and night, without a solution. Zhang, passionate in her affair, had a strange idea. She thought that her daughter, Qindi, was 28 years old and had a pleasant appearance. Disregarding her own flesh and blood, she pawned Qindi to a prostitute house run by a Zhou in No. 306 Baoyu Lane, Dongxin Bridge, French Concession, for two years, receiving 160 yuan, which she gave to Wang to invest in his business in order to improve it. After entering the brothel, Qindi was escorted to the streets every night by prostitutes and servants to receive guests. If she slightly offended the madam, she would be severely beaten and suffered greatly. She longed to escape from the pit of fire but had no opportunity. Until about 7 PM the other day, she took advantage of the staff's inattention to escape and rushed to her aunt Zhu Zhang's house at No. 40 Dong Tangjia Lane, asking for help and spending the night. Around 7 AM yesterday morning, her aunt planned to send her to her sister, but Qindi refused and cried loudly. The incident was heard by police officer Li Zhenxiang, who was on duty at the Fourth Post, who came and took Qindi to the First Branch of the Third District. During the preliminary hearing by the station chief, Qindi tearfully recounted the events and asked for a fair judgment. Chief Jin, astonished that there could be such terrible parents in the world, immediately sent police to summon Zhang, and then wrote a document to report to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Male Corpse Found Murdered on Tianbao Road

Countless Knife Wounds and Bloody Mess

Yesterday, a male corpse was found murdered on the wasteland between Tianbao Road and Qimei Road in Hongkou. The body was about thirty years old and quite tall. He was wearing a padded jacket and trousers, tied white socks, black shoes, and a tweed overcoat. His attire was mismatched, indicating that he was not a respectable person. His head was covered with countless knife wounds, a bloody mess and a terrible sight. The area was very remote. A passerby discovered the body and reported it to the Third Branch of the Fifth District, which ordered the police to investigate but found no family. The 16th Tu local head was ordered to report to the court for an autopsy.

Girl Crushed to Death by Car on Gonghe Road

Near Gonghe Road and Huasheng Road in Zhabei, at 11:30 AM yesterday, a cargo truck with license plate Hua Zhao 3443 struck a girl when it failed to stop in time. The wheels crushed her left leg bone, and her right leg was also seriously injured, bleeding profusely. Police officer Liu Fengge from the 14th Post took the injured girl and the driver to the station. The girl was first sent to the Pushan Hospital for treatment. The driver, Yan Shaobo, 24 years old, from Tongzhou, who lives at No. 875 Wangjia Lane, Kangnaituo Road in the Concession, and drives for the Tongshang Automobile Company at No. 113 Xinzha Road, admitted to hitting the girl. The injured girl's mother, Chen Zhangshi, 29 years old, from Funing, who lives in a small lane on Gonghe Road, also reported to the police. The girl was her daughter, Xiao Liaotou, six years old. Later, the girl died of her injuries before she could be treated. The case was submitted to the bureau for investigation.

Autopsy of Detective Who Died in the Line of Duty

The day before yesterday at 10 AM, a thief fled into a lane in Hexing Lane, Wuzhou Road. At that time, Zhu Jitang, a Chinese detective No. 294 of the Lao Zha Police Station, attempted to arrest him, but the thief opened fire, hitting a vital spot and causing his death. The thief was also shot and wounded by detective Zhu and captured. The news was reported in yesterday's newspaper. Subsequently, the Jia Yu Road Police Station received the report and dispatched Chinese and Western detectives to transport the body of Zhu, who died in the line of duty, to the forensic examination office on Feilun Road. The wounded thief was sent to the Municipal Council Hospital for treatment. Yesterday morning, Zhan Liangce, the prosecutor delegated by the First Special District Court, and judicial medical recorder Wang Zuyi, arrived at the office to examine the body and took statements. Detective No. 1874 stated that a Westerner told him that there was a thief in front. After hearing this, he immediately chased after the thief to Hexing Lane on Wuzhou Road and saw the thief fighting with a plainclothes detective. He then drew his gun and fired at the thief. Detective No. 3322 stated that he was also present at the time and fired a shot, but he did not know if it hit. The deceased's wife, Zhu Wu, 35 years old, stated that the deceased was her husband, and she was cooking when the incident occurred, so she did not know the details. The Western police chief of the police station reported that the deceased's parents were still in Tianjin, and the colleagues of the Lao Zha Police Station were willing to contribute funds to buy a coffin and requested that the coffin be temporarily placed in the office until his family arrived in Shanghai and the police station had prepared for the funeral. Mr. Zhan approved the request and ordered that the body of Zhu Jitang, male, had died from head injuries sustained during his lifetime, and the body should be handed over to his wife, Zhu Wu, for burial.

Digging Up Official Seals to Cure Illness

Unbelievably Foolish

Yesterday at 12 PM, someone was digging out official seals from the Municipal Public Security Bureau's notice banning small gambling and the Garrison Headquarters' notice banning gambling that were posted on the bulletin board at Xiaobeimen with a small pocket knife, and hiding them on their body. The act was spotted by Liu Zhongheng, the patrol leader of the First Branch of the Second District, who asked why he was doing so. The person claimed that he was using them to cure illness. Fearing forgery and the crime of tearing down official documents, Patrol Leader Liu immediately took him to the station for questioning. Shen, the station chief, questioned him and learned that his name was Li Fa Lu, from Yangzhou, and he lived at No. 25 Chenyi Lane, Xin Taigu Road. His daughter was sick and could not be cured. He went to the Zizhu Nunnery in the Eight Immortals Bridge to pray for a prescription. He was told that she was possessed by an evil spirit and needed two official seals to suppress it to heal. He was anxious to cure her illness and had nowhere to find seals, so someone pointed him to the notices. He had no other intention. The officer, realizing his foolishness, lightly fined him two yuan and kept the seals on file.

Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway Asks the County to Protect Traffic

The Shanghai County Government recently approved a letter from the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway Engineering Department, stating that since the opening of the railway, residents along the route have been crowding around whenever they see vehicles passing, eager to watch. Some even stand in the road. Children are especially dangerous, deliberately crossing the road when cars pass or throwing mud, sand, and stones as a game. Even worse, during the day, they place obstacles on the road to block traffic, and at night, they pull up and reverse the signposts and signals along the road. Such unwarranted damage to public property is deplorable. If measures are not taken to prohibit this, the consequences will be unimaginable. It is proposed to clearly explain the dangers of the road and the protection of public property. At the same time, instruct each public security bureau to add posts in the station area to prevent and maintain road administration. In addition to separate letters, the corresponding letters are sent to your government for reference, hoping to immediately instruct compliance.

Large Quantity of Red Pills Seized on Small Steamboat

At 8:10 PM the other night, Chinese detectives No. 7 and No. 101 of the Customs Water Patrol boarded a boat to patrol the Jinliyuan Wharf area of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. The captain of the Changfu Steamboat saw the detectives and, feeling guilty, reversed the boat to escape. The two detectives were unable to catch up and hid in a dark place to wait. At 9:40 PM, they saw the steamboat returning from afar and docking outside the Jiangyu Steamboat. They boarded the steamboat and seized four items that looked like luggage. Upon opening them, they found they were all red pills, a kind of narcotic, totaling thirty large packages (three hundred small boxes, each worth about eight or nine yuan), worth over two thousand yuan. On suspicion of smuggling prohibited items, they immediately took the captain Yao Zhangsheng, crew members Zhang Jintao, Shen Jintao, Ye Changgen, and Yao Yinbao, along with the steamboat, to the police station. Yao confessed that three people had hired him to transport the four pieces of luggage to the Jiangyu Steamboat at 8 PM that afternoon, and he did not know they contained narcotics. After questioning, the police chief ordered that the red pills be sent to Customs for destruction, and Yao and the other four were handed over to detective Qu Hejin for transfer to the court for interrogation yesterday afternoon. The steamboat was impounded pending further instructions from higher authorities.

Lawsuit Over Lion Cat Cigarette Premium Gifts

Salesman Accused of Fraud

Released on Bail of 40,000 Yuan

Ford Tobacco Company, in an effort to expand sales of its Lion Cat brand cigarettes, adopted the current commercial practice of offering premium gifts, with the value of the gift determined by the quantity sold. Gongxing Tobacco Store in Jinyang Temple Lane, Hangzhou, which specializes in the sale of various cigarettes, learned that the premium gift program offered by Ford was exceptionally generous, and the gifts were valuable. They entered into a sales contract with Wu Yinting, the Ford manager from Shaoxing, and made great efforts to promote sales. In a short time, they sold over 812 cases, earning gifts worth over 40,000 yuan, which were held by Ford. Last month, Ford shipped 320 cases of Lion Cat cigarettes to Hangzhou for sale, valued at 41,420 yuan. Yang Shengyuan, the store owner, believed that this amount roughly equaled the value of the premium gifts, intending to offset the two to clear the transaction. He did not pay for the goods. However, Wu Yinting refused to pay the required expenses and went to Hangzhou to demand payment but did not receive any money. The other day, he learned that Yang Shengyuan had come to Shanghai from Hangzhou and was staying at Room 69 of the Jue Lu Hotel on Xizang Road. He reported to the Lao Zha Police Station, claiming that Gongxing Tobacco Store had closed and Yang Shengyuan had fraudulently taken money. The police chief sent detective Chen Yonggui and Western detective Klein to the Jue Lu Hotel, where they arrested Yang. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the First Special District Court, where Judge Zhang Junqing interrogated them. The defendant hired lawyer Chen Tingrui to defend him, claiming that it was because Ford Company did not provide the premium gifts that were due, so the defendant had to deduct the cigarette price. There was no fraud. The facts were clear. Moreover, Gongxing Tobacco Store was still operating as usual, and the defendant was a man of great wealth. The plaintiff's arbitrary accusation requested that the defendant be released on bail and that a lawsuit be filed against Kang for false accusations after the matter was investigated. Qian Xunjiu, the police lawyer, stated that he had no objection to the defendant's application for bail. The defendant also presented a letter from Wang Xiaozhu, chairman of the Shanghai Business Association, proving everything. Judge Zhang then ordered that the defendant Yang Shengyuan be released on bail of 40,000 yuan, pending further investigation.

Trade Association News

New Medicine Trade Association: Yesterday, a temporary members' meeting was held, attended by over thirty people. Chairman Zhang Xianda and Sun Choucheng reported on the situation of refugees from Northeast China in Shanghai. Discussions then commenced, resulting in a decision that each pharmacy present would commit to a monthly donation (limited to six months). Representatives would be sent to pharmacies that did not attend to solicit donations. All donated funds would be collected by the association and deposited in a bank for safekeeping. Regarding pharmaceuticals, it was decided that once the relief team had left the hospital, the association would directly deliver the appropriate items to the relevant military unit for their use. The meeting then proceeded to discuss other matters before adjourning.

Restaurant and Bar Industry: The Trade Association held an executive committee meeting yesterday afternoon at three o'clock. Chairman Cheng Keshen presided over the meeting, discussing the following matters: 1) Regarding the illegal formation of an association by the catering industry, which was falsely using the association's name to collect membership fees privately, a request was submitted to the Social Bureau for investigation and suppression to ensure compliance with regulations. On the second of this month, a reply was received, stating that the matter was noted, and the preparatory committee of the Shanghai Catering Industry Trade Association was strictly ordered to conclude and dissolve within ten days and to merge with this association as members. Acknowledgment was requested. Following this order, the discussion focused on dispatching representatives to handle the takeover. It was resolved to appoint standing committee members Hu Yuantang and Zhang Shaoping, along with catering industry leader Gu Yuexiang, to negotiate the takeover and merger. 2) Cheng Kefan reported on the dispute over winter liquor license taxes. After discussions at a meeting of nine industry representatives, a general meeting was scheduled to be convened, and this association should participate in a unified action. It was resolved to pass the motion. 3) Regarding relief for banditry-stricken areas in Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, and donations to the Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army, it was resolved to proceed accordingly. The association would send donation lists to each member for voluntary contributions. 4) The industry regulations, based on thirteen draft articles, were amended and approved, and a request was submitted to the Social Bureau for record-keeping. It was resolved to pass the motion. 5) Regarding the association's funding issues, a further letter would be sent to the finance department urging the prompt collection of funds. It was resolved to pass the motion, and the meeting adjourned.

Cotton Cloth Industry: The Trade Union held its fourth joint meeting of the executive and supervisory committees yesterday afternoon at three o'clock. Chairman Xia Xianting presided over the meeting, resolving the following matters: 1) Regarding the revision of standard contract forms for foreign firms, it was resolved to approve the amendments and send a letter to the Shanghai Cotton Grade Piece Goods Import Association for consultation and signing. 2) The Textile Merchants Association notified the union that Article 7 of the Trade Union Law had been amended to "Companies and firms in the same industry should all be members of the same industry trade association." Regarding how the union should promote membership among non-member businesses, it was resolved to begin with an investigation. 3) The Municipal Chamber of Commerce advocated for monthly donations for Northeast refugees. It was resolved to send a circular to all industry members, encouraging them to actively recognize and donate. In addition to this, the union would first pledge a police donation of one thousand yuan, to be delivered to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce for remittance to the Northeast for relief. 4) Regarding the Chinese Aviation Construction Association's request for membership, it was resolved to approve the application. In addition to replying to the association and sending a membership fee of one hundred yuan, a notice would be sent to industry members encouraging them to join freely. Tobacco and Alcohol Industry: The Shanghai South Office of the Trade Association is currently dealing with increasingly complex matters related to disputes over tobacco and alcohol license taxes, and guiding the implementation of stamp duties. The original office building at 381 Fumin Road is insufficient for its needs. It has already relocated to a house at number 27 on Zhonghua Road near the south end of the road, and the office has moved in yesterday.
